## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) is determined by restoring forces (dependent on position x), damping forces (dependent on velocity v), and possibly external driving (dependent on time t). The task seeks the equation of motion in the form dv/dt = f(x, v, t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - x**2) * v + c1 * x (nonlinear damping with amplitude-dependent sign)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * Abs(x) (asymmetric nonlinear restoring)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic velocity-dependent damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinear restoring force)
- Mixed nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (general polynomial restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (forced linear oscillator with phase)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power restoring terms (x²) → asymmetric potential, indicating broken symmetry like Helmholtz oscillator
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x²)·v → self-sustained oscillations with limit cycles (Van der Pol type)
- Cubic position terms (x³) with same/opposite sign as linear term → hardening/softening spring behavior (Duffing type)
- Sinusoidal time dependence → external periodic driving or parametric excitation; look for cos(c·t) or sin(c·t)
- Odd powers of velocity (v, v³) → energy dissipation or injection depending on sign (Rayleigh-type damping)
- Product terms x·v → position-dependent damping, common in nonlinear friction models
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence indicates forced/parametric oscillation

**GT:** `-0.721004*v*(1 - v²) - 1.03737*v - 2.44077*x*(0.015413*|v|^(1/3) + 1)`

Simplifying: `-1.75838*v + 0.721004*v³ - 2.44077*x - 0.037621*x*|v|^(1/3)`

The key terms are:
1. Linear in v: `c*v`
2. Cubic in v: `c*v³`
3. Linear in x: `c*x`
4. **Critical term:** `c*x*|v|^(1/3)` — this involves `x` multiplied by a fractional power of `|v|`

This `x*|v|^(1/3)` term is very unusual. Let me check each candidate for the ability to produce this term.

Most candidates have polynomial terms in v and x (like `v*x`, `v*x²`, `v²*x`, `x³`, etc.) or trigonometric/exponential terms. None of these can produce `|v|^(1/3)`.

The only candidates with potentially flexible nonlinear functions of v are those with `exp(c*v²)` terms (candidates 6-9, 11, 18, 23, 31, 33, 45, etc.). Let me check if `x*exp(c3*v²)` could approximate `x*(constant + small*|v|^(1/3))`.

However, `exp(c3*v²)` is an even function of v and smooth, but it cannot exactly equal `a + b*|v|^(1/3)` for any choice of c3. The exponential function and the fractional power `|v|^(1/3)` are fundamentally different functional forms.

Similarly, `cos(c*x²)` terms can't help with the v-dependence.

The rational forms like `x/(c1 + x²)` also can't produce the `|v|^(1/3)` dependence.

Let me check candidates with `|v|` or `Abs(v)` terms:
- **Candidate 11:** has `c9*v*Abs(v)` = `c9*|v|*v` — this is `v|v|`, not `|v|^(1/3)*x`
- **Candidate 16:** has `c9*v*Abs(v)` — same issue
- **Candidate 37:** has `c9*v*Abs(v)` — same issue
- **Candidate 4:** has `c9*x*Abs(x)` — this involves `|x|`, not `|v|`
- **Candidate 25:** has `c9*x*Abs(x)` — same
- **Candidate 40:** has `c8*x*Abs(x)` — same
- **Candidate 46:** has `c9*x*Abs(x)` — same
- **Candidate 24:** has `c8*x*Abs(x)` — same

None of these have `x*|v|^(1/3)` or anything that could match it.

The term `x*|v|^(1/3)` with coefficient ~0.0376 is small but nonzero. No candidate formula contains a term that could produce this fractional power of |v| multiplied by x. 

Even though the coefficient is small (~0.0376 compared to ~2.44 for the x term), it's still a structurally distinct term that cannot be generated by any of the candidate formulas' functional forms. The candidates only have integer powers of v (v, v², v³) multiplied by powers of x, exponentials of v², or absolute values of v or x to integer-like powers.

None of the candidates can exactly reproduce `|v|^(1/3)*x`.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
-0.721004421988058*v*(1 - v**2) - 1.03737009496134*v - 2.44077135428351*x*(0.0154128049692563*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1)
```

Expanding:
```
-0.721004*v + 0.721004*v**3 - 1.03737*v - 2.44077*x*0.015413*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 2.44077*x
```

Simplifying:
```
-1.75837*v + 0.721004*v**3 - 2.44077*x - 0.037623*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)
```

The key basis functions in the GT are:
1. **v** (linear in v)
2. **v³** (cubic in v)
3. **x** (linear in x)
4. **x·|v|^(1/3)** (x times a fractional power of |v|)

The term `x·|v|^(1/3)` is crucial and unusual. No polynomial or standard elementary function combination can replicate `|v|^(1/3)` exactly.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of this `|v|^(1/3)` term or something that could produce it.

**Key observation:** None of the candidates contain `Abs(v)**(1/3)` or `|v|^(1/3)`. The candidates use terms like:
- Polynomials in x, v
- `cos(c*t)`, `cos(c*x²)`
- `exp(c*v²)`
- `Abs(v)`, `Abs(x)`
- Rational functions in x
- `x/(c + x²)` type terms

The term `x·|v|^(1/3)` cannot be represented by any of these basis functions. Let me verify:

- `exp(c*v²)` cannot equal `|v|^(1/3)` for any constant c
- `cos(c*x²)` doesn't involve v
- Polynomials in v cannot produce `|v|^(1/3)`
- `v*Abs(v)` = `|v|^2 * sign(v)` ≠ `|v|^(1/3)`
- `Abs(v)` = `|v|` ≠ `|v|^(1/3)`
- Rational functions of x don't help with the v dependence

The coefficient of the `x·|v|^(1/3)` term is approximately -0.0376, which is small but nonzero. Since we cannot set GT constants to zero (they are fixed), this term must be present in any matching candidate.

Since **no candidate** contains a term that can produce `x·|v|^(1/3)`, none can be exactly equivalent to the GT.

Let me verify this is not negligible - the GT constants are FIXED, and the coefficient ~0.0376 is nonzero. Per the rules, we need EXACT mathematical equivalence, not approximations.

Going through all 50 candidates systematically: every single one lacks the ability to produce the `|v|^(1/3)` term. The candidates use polynomial powers of v (v, v², v³), `Abs(v)`, `v*Abs(v)`, `exp(c*v²)`, but none have fractional powers of |v|.
